commit d51a44946fa3d5bd322462824f4d9ae596346045
Author: jverkoey <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 16 10:33:00 2011 -0800

    [UI] Revert network request changes for the web view controller.
    
    Adding support for network status isn't as simple as it might seem
    for this controller. If the controller is popped off the stack,
    for example, we'll never get enough request stopped messages to
    stop the indicator, resulting in a permanent loading state for the
    app.
    
    Barring a proper solution to this problem, for now we'll leave it
    to the controller to display the fact that it is loading.

commit 4c96f31fa11c974dfa6cb1d33c0be16ed60c63a0
Author: wbailey <wi11.bai1ey@facebook.com>
Date:   Thu Dec 9 09:25:11 2010 -0800

    Adding a TTTableViewNetworkEnabledDelegate
    
    TTTableViewNetworkEnabledDelegate provides support for both drag refresh
    and the new infinite scroll footer. You can choose to enable either,
    both or neither of these features when you instantiate the delegate. The
    delegate header also defines the
    TTTableNetworkEnabledTableViewController protocol, which allows
    TableViewControllers to specify when infinite scroll loading should
    occur based on a scroll ratio by implementing shouldLoadAtScrollRatio:

    [UI] Ensure TTSearchDisplayController hides the overlay view when searches complete.
    
    This fixes a bug where the error overlay view is not hidden when the
    search is cancelled.
    This happens currently when you try to search without a network
    connection. The error overlay remains after the search is dismissed.

    the search controller; however, in order to synchronize the animations
    with the search fade out and to handle this globally going forward I
    think it's better to fix this in three20.
    
    Test Plan:
    verified that the overlay view is now hidden when the search
    is cancelled

commit 8a9fde5c4ca0a46ef0c619705ef54b4b5f0db1ef
Author: Cemal Eker <hello@cemaleker.com>
Date:   Thu Nov 4 19:35:08 2010 +0200

    [UI] Fixed a bug caused by touchesEnded event not being received.
    
    UIKit sometime couldn't deliver messages for UIResponder properly.
    That causes application to crash when application can't receive
    "touches ended" and later tries to reach ended and released UITouch
    object. I implemented proper retaining for UITouch objects. And
    also I implemented an ensure touches method which checks touch
    phases and release them if ended and we couldn't receive ending
    message somehow.
    
    Solution for the issue discussed here:
    http://discussions.apple.com/message.jspa?messageID=7139722
    
    Closes #320

commit bf21707015c962890b0ebc676d2b958da711ef00
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Thu May 13 16:51:27 2010 -0700

    TTTableView should preserve first responder across -reloadData
    
    -[UITableView reloadData] wipes out first responder status, and this can cause
    the keyboard to disappear for no apparent reason, if for example you're typing
    in a text field that's inside the table. Remember the first responder and
    restore it after calling super.

commit 351089235aedc523d7e82683ed2de7586bb073f9
Author: wbailey <wi11.bai1ey@facebook.com>
Date:   Sun Oct 31 12:04:15 2010 -0700

    [Network] Fix bug in TTURLCache storeImage total pixel count calculations.
    
    I was debugging why images just added get expired immediately once you
    reach the image cache max pixels. Debugging statements revealed that
    although there were no images in the cache map the pixel count was still
    just below the max after each expiration.
    
    It seems the problem here is that when storeImage:forURL:force: is
    called it's not accounting for the possibility that the image is already
    in the cache. It always increments the pixelCount even though there may
    already be an image in the dictionary with that key. This causes the
    pixelCount to grow higher than it actually is.
    
    This change checks for an existing image in the cache when storing at a
    key and decrements the pixel count and removes instances from the sorted
    array before continuing to add the image back to the cache. This ensures
    that the pixel count is correct and that there are not duplicates in the
    sorted list, while still maintaining the appropriate LRU cache behavior.
    
    Test Plan: added conditional log statements and verified that the cache
    was behaving appropriately also noted images are now staying the cache
    properly rather than immediately expiring once the max is reached.

commit 16282d004e8de84f8687a8f2611e94930f8d0e03
Author: Paulo Oliveira <Paulo@112-235-191-190.cab.prima.net.ar>
Date:   Wed Jul 21 17:08:14 2010 -0300

    [UI] TTScrollView Improvements.
    
    With this improvement we're almost identical to the iPhone Photo Album functionalities:
    
    * Add zoom in/out based on the velocity that the fingers move on the pinch gesture.
    * Add zoom in/out from or to the center of fingers on every zoom level.
    * Add residual movement with deceleration after the user lifts their finger when dragging zoomed images.
    
    New zoom engine also include a few convenient properties and public methods:
    
    * Allows define the rate of deceleration after the user lifts their finger. (property).
    
    * Allows to set the maximum scale factor that can be applied to the scroll view's content. (property).
    
    * Allows to set the current zoom scale. Optionally animated, and optionally specifying the anchor point (methods).

    [UI] A bunch of tweaks to the drag refresh table header
    
    - Changed the external interface to the DragRefreshView to be just
      -setStatus:. There's no need to have external clients managing the flipped
      state of the image and the visibility of the activity indicator. The view
      should manage all this itself.

      view has this.

      request completed.
    
    - Renamed one of the state enum constants for consistency.
    
    This is a net loss of code for arguably greater cleanliness and functionality.

commit 893a1f7ceafc02197aa6446f4968b74cdcecf9d5
Author: beng <beng@facebook.com>
Date:   Wed Jun 30 20:07:36 2010 -0700

    [Style] Real fix for Asian styled text layout issues
    
    Summary:
    Here's the correct fix for Asian styled text layout issues.
    
    My previous workaround worked for a few cases where the text was mostly
    Latin, but it wasn't the correct fix for the underlying problem.
    
    The actual problem was that -[NSString drawInRect:withFont:] naively
    defaults to UILineBreakModeWordWrap, even if it can't wrap in the
    height it's given.
    
    When using UILineBreakModeWordWrap, this method prefers to try to word
    wrap (and fail) than to condense the text to fit on a single line,
    which is how TTStyledLayout assumes -[NSString drawInRect:withFont:]
    works.
    
    To fix this issue, we now explicitly specify the behavior we want
    (UILineBreakModeClip -- truncate if the text doesn't fit in the rect),
    which convinces NSString to condense the text to fit inside the rect.
    
    Testing:
    Reproduced Korean truncation issue by visiting a profile
    in simulator and on phone (OS 4).
    
    Applied fix, confirmed in simulator and on phone that truncation issue
    was fixed.
    
    Reviewed By: oyamauchi

commit 2607677769203c82a3adec73db84912d66e6411d
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Wed Jul 7 21:06:06 2010 -0700

    [UINavigator] Persist navigation stack when the app is backgrounded (multitasking)
    
    The ApplicationWillTerminate notification may not be posted when the app is quit
    while it's in the background, so we have to treat being backgrounded as if the
    app is terminating.
    
    Unfortunately, there is no way to behave gracefully on OS versions prior to 4.0
    except by passing the notification name as a string (not as a constant which
    points to said string). There's no way to stop the dynamic linker from trying to
    resolve that symbol.

commit f02edf6b03a8bc6294a9eb88739bae2f490012c0
Author: beng <beng@facebook.com>
Date:   Fri May 14 10:49:21 2010 -0700

    [Core] Use day name in short date strings only for dates <= 5 days ago
    
    Summary:
    Previously, when formatting a date, we would use the day name for any
    date that was <= 60 * 24 * 7 seconds ago (one week's worth of
    seconds).
    
    This was really confusing for dates that were just short a week's worth
    of seconds ago: if today is Friday, and the item we're formatting was
    almost a week ago (but also on Friday), it would show up as "Fri".
    
    Now, we'll use 5 days' worth of seconds as the cut-off to use
    day names. That way, weekends will still work, but you won't see
    "Fri" for things that happened last Friday.
    
    Test Plan:
    Using a table view with items with dates in it, confirmed
    previously an item with a date of just short of 60 * 24 * 7 seconds
    ago was rendered as "Fri XX:XX AM".
    
    Applied my fix, now it's rendered as "May 7 XX:XX AM".

Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 22 19:25:12 2010 -0700

    [Core] Remove hard-coding in number format localization.
    
    TTFormatInteger() was committing the cardinal sin of hardcoding a
    localizable aspect of a number format. I traced it to a commit that
    claimed this line of code was necessary to get the comma to show up,
    which is NOT TRUE and actively works against localization of number
    formatting. The grouping separator is not the same in all locales.

    fr_FR and make sure the result is 1.024.

commit 72af2909f11fbe36d0d91fb6bc298a874535302a
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jun 4 18:23:05 2010 -0400

    [Three20] Remove the composite lib from the Three20 project.
    
    Compositing the library was causing build problems when making universal
    binaries. It seems that, in general, compositing libraries together should
    be avoided due to the strangeness of multiple architectures being linked
    together, for one.
    
    This is going to cause a bit of pain for anyone using the library due
    to the fact that they will now need to add each library to their project
    individually. If there is an alternate solution, it will be much preferred.

commit c078d6f76691a57ea2b8b8a6b888914a1d436f9c

commit eae95b567967dee679ed4ef4d3a497a07323f2c9
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 22 17:35:05 2010 -0700

    [Network] Remove appended strings from the etag.
    
    Some etags sent from the server include appended text, such as -gzip
    when the request is gzipped. The etag spec requires that etags be
    defined as a key inside of a pair of quotes, and nothing else.
    
    With that in light, we find the quoted key in the etag and only cache
    that value.
    
    This has been tested with gzipped twitter requests and correctly
    returns a 304 when used with just the key (sans -gzip suffix).

commit 3c10fc026c96de3f53f1f0d5e32291cdf543b45b
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 22 17:18:49 2010 -0700

    [Network] Once we receive the data response, cache the etag value.
    
    This is step 1 as previously noted in
    1df995bc4b55aa7a574b2315837805f4fb78d877.

commit c05f01772951dadb59c033dc1a0205b9656bcd09
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 22 16:55:54 2010 -0700

    [Network] Use the cached etag value when sending the request.
    
    Left to do:
    1) We need to store the resulting etag value once the request
       has been received.
    2) Once we store the key, the next time we send a request it will
       include the most recent etag. On the next request, assuming the
       server data hasn't changed, we'll get a 302.
    3) We then need to properly handle the 302 response.
    4) Done! Now for testing.

commit 1df92e80219db1b2bcfe9a014cf7ed213bde8be4
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 22 16:48:39 2010 -0700

    [Network] Add etag support to the TTURLCache.
    
    Etags are stored as key/value pairs, where the key is the file name,
    and the value is the file data. The key is the same cache key used
    for a given URL, and the etag path will be in a subdirectory of the
    cache titled "etag".

commit cc1fad3004eb15b803dd19f7b1e7d2077c9619af

    [Network] Add the etag when we create the request.
    
    Instead of waiting for the connection callback, we'll add the etag
    when we create the NSURLRequest (much more sensical).

commit 780b98455718138fc2e645a5d798c4531ae766f8
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 20 19:52:31 2010 -0700

    Add +Additions library header files.
    
    The goal: to eventually phase out the global namespace polluting of
    the Three20 additions.
    
    Three20.h currently still contains all Three20 additions. In one
    month's time, they will all be removed. If you make use of any
    Three20 additions (view.width, for example), then you have three
    options:
    
    1) Switch to the new Three20+Additions.h library header file.
    2) Keep using Three20.h, but explicitly add the necessary addition
       headers.
    3) Update your code to stop using Three20 additions.
    
    1 is a pretty minimal change that won't impact your code. 2 will
    require a little bit of sleuthing to determine which files need
    which additions. 3 is outright painful and not suggested.
    
    On May 20, 2010, all addition header files will be removed from
    Three20.h and Three20Core.h.

commit 7c03000aa8af3577cfe5a5eccca813abcca24e2d
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Apr 18 01:29:13 2010 -0400

    Use correct initializer format throughout Three20.
    
    From the Apple Docs, if you override an init method, you need to
    call the super class's designated initializer and assign the result
    to self. You should then return self (or nil, if the method failed).
    
    Testing: Built TTCatalog and navigated through each section.
    
    Notes: No logic was changed in this commit, strictly-speaking. The
    code has simply been made more "correct" by Apple's documentation.

commit 4968eaaf4b0cc070f380a69e365ec931cd2b6f5f
Author: Brian Chapados <chapados@sciencegeeks.org>
Date:   Tue Feb 16 10:07:18 2010 -0800

    [Nib] Only create a view in -loadView if no nib-based view is present.
    
    The default UIViewController#loadView method will load a a view from a
    nib file if one is present and connected to the view outlet.  If a nib
    is present, the 'nibName' propery will be set to a non-nil value.
    
    According to Apple, if you're loading your view from a nib, you should
    not override loadView, so we mimic the default -loadView behavior by
    exiting if a nib-based view is present.

Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 29 17:32:55 2010 -0700

    Fix the popup view controller issue
    
    Adds a method to UIViewController which allows it to express whether
    it should ever be considered the "top" view controller, and added a
    check to -[TTNavigator topViewController] to respect this. Defaults to
    YES in UIViewController; the only override for now is
    TTPopupViewController, which overrides to NO. In future, we can have
    subclasses of TTPopupViewController re-override it to YES if need be.
    
    Tested the camera button in the FB app's publisher bar (on the device)
    and verified that the action sheet buttons do what they're supposed
    to. Also tried the action sheet buttons for the Profile action sheet
    (button in top right corner of friend's profile).
    
    Review request: 73

commit d66d2697c0c057b4dc9585316a49a660ae53b367
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 29 17:06:00 2010 -0700

    Fix keyboard-disappearing resizing issue
    
    This task of TTViewControllers auto-resizing for keyboard changes is
    fraught with peril. In this instance, the problem was appearing in a
    couple of places in the FB app. When logging in, the controller
    displayed immediately after the login controller (the feed controller)
    was getting -keyboardWillDisappear: (because it was disappearing from
    the login screen) and was resizing itself to be the keyboard's height
    taller than the screen. Another place was in search: when drilling
    into a controller from a search listing with the keyboard up, the new
    controller would again be the keyboard's height taller than the
    screen. This change fixes that and also corrects a possible
    double-initialization of the table view, resulting from accessor
    properties actually being methods that initialize the ivar in
    question. See the comment. >_<

commit bd50f1c031b8c02cbb472493e39ef2604837e267
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 24 15:03:36 2010 -0700

    Make UIViewAdditions methods for showing as keyboard send right notifications
    
    I recently changed TTViewController to correctly handle
    UIKeyboard{Will,Did}{Show,Hide}Notifications, and without this change, table
    view that autoresized for the keyboard were broken when some other view was
    displayed as the keyboard. This makes the relevant code in UIViewAdditions send
    the correct notifications so it really does act like a keyboard appearing and
    disappearing.

commit b802482806de233ac7b34737d62f85db54d56a17
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>

    Give TTTableMoreButton its own model ivar
    
    This allows you to use the more button in a table view where the model you want
    to refresh is not the table view's data source's model. For example, you might
    have a table view with two sections, each showing different models.

commit a87a9077e02c6f03f252f5b04a1c07be96130648
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 15 20:34:46 2010 -0700

    Use DidShow and DidHide keyboard notifications instead of custom hacks
    
    There are actually official notifications of when the keyboard is finished
    hiding and showing, so use those instead of using timers with guessed
    delays. Also, use the symbols for the notification names instead of strings.
    
    This fixes the bug wherein the keyboard events arrive in a weird order when the
    first responder changes from one control to another immediately. Previously it
    went will-disappear, will-appear, did-disappear, did-appear, which doesn't make
    sense. Now, it goes will-disappear, will-appear, did-appear -- i.e. it doesn't
    lie and say the keyboard disappeared fully, and the events arrive in a sensible
    order.
    
    There is still some weird behavior specific to table view controllers
    (willDisappear sets the frame and then it immediately gets reset in -didAppear,
    causing some weird jumping) but that's for a separate change.

commit 95707ce9f835be6f5869b1a2936127fbe3c03d5d
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Sat Mar 13 19:12:06 2010 -0800

    Fix -[UIImage(TTCategory) transformWidth:height:rotate:] "invalid context"
    
    This method is meant to resize an image, but it was using the wrong value for
    the bytesPerRow of the new image (it wasn't taking into account the fact that
    the image is being resized -- facepalm). The bug would only manifest if the
    destination size was bigger than the image's current size, because the value
    given for the new image's bytesPerRow would be too small. If the image was being
    scaled down, it would work properly, but some memory would be wasted because the
    new image's bytesPerRow would be bigger than necessary. Sigh.
    
    I also wrote a brief doc comment for the method while I was at it.

commit f778238242097b425d50ce95175baf774aee6b51
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 18 13:12:19 2010 -0800

    Add a new TTNavigator delegate method allowing modification of URLs to open
    
    The new method is a superset of -navigator:shouldOpenURL: which allows the
    navigator's delegate to prevent opening of a URL. The new method actually
    returns the URL to open (or nil to prevent), which allows the delegate to modify
    the URL to open.
    
    I considered deprecating -navigator:shouldOpenURL: but I actually don't think
    that's necessary since it's more convenient (and semantically clearer) to
    implement that instead of -navigator:URLToOpen: if you don't need the
    modification functionality.
    
    Also, I have an Xcode plugin that strips trailing whitespace, which is why the
    huge amount of changes to these files. To see the actual changes, do "git show
    -b".

    Deprecate the weak/strong methods in TTUserInfo.

    that are still occurring. This is an intermediary change to allow people
    to update to the new methods gracefully.

commit 7183db6054c572a921287089e15abc3f50301b23
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 3 16:28:17 2010 -0500

    Allow collision keys in the XML parser in order to support RSS feeds.
    
    RSS feeds tend to allow their feed items to be placed in the channel
    object as flat items, instead of within an array. The original XML parser
    implementation assumed that keys were always unique, but this is not the
    case with RSS feeds. Options were added to make it possible to toggle this
    functionality.

commit d67b2d245b86d96873733482e28cc821203ffb9e
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Thu Jan 21 20:06:53 2010 -0800

    Reduce include scope of TTDebugFlags.h
    
    The fact that TTDebugFlags.h was included in TTGlobalCore.h meant that every
    time you changed a debug flag, the entire project had to be rebuilt. This change
    makes it so that only the files that use a debug flag have to be rebuilt, which
    cuts build times and generally makes using these things more pleasant.

commit b6aae48a7b5b4d0e74f74595dd9f8a1cb9c74d5f
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 18 14:50:01 2009 -0800

    [Network] Thread-safe TTNetworkRequestStarted/Stopped.
    
    The TTNetworkRequestStarted/Stopped methods in the global network
    header are now thread safe and throw an exception when you attempt
    to stop more requests than you've started.
    
    This does not solve the problem of not calling stop enough times.
    A fix for this that doesn't involve a large amount of overengineering
    is not immediately obvious.
    
    Some considered alternatives for debugging:
     - A watchdog that periodically checks for active network connections.

commit ffea6a8b3fdd7cfefa187e270638b2ca47e91be4
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Dec 4 19:43:26 2009 -0800

    [Debug] Deprecate the TTLOG macro using a compiler deprecation flag.
    
    You'll now start receiving warnings if you're still using TTLOG.
    Please run a global find-replace of TTLOG => TTDINFO.
    
    TTD* macros are an improvement over the simple TTLOG macro.
     * They don't leave the log strings in the code in Release builds
     * More contextual information (filename + line number)
     * Debug assertions
     * Multiple logging levels
     * Conditional logging

commit 93124e72cdcf517c1c679d5cd5964c5d71e920a7
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Nov 20 02:53:54 2009 -0800

    [UnitTests] Add unit testing target to Three20.
    
    From this point on we will be building unit tests for Three20, starting
    with the core library components. The unit test target will be marked
    as a dependency of the Three20 library so that every time you build Three20,
    the unit tests also run.
    
    There isn't a strict concept of "running" a unit test in Xcode. Instead you
    simply build the unit test target and the tests are performed automatically.
    If any tests fail, you will receive a build error-like notification with a
    descriptive message.
    
    New Unit Tests
    * NSDataAdditions
      -(NSString*)md5hash;

commit cf8d192635a44c27bcdc9efe02b3f88f6db169a3
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Dec 9 16:46:23 2009 -0800

    TTURLRequestDelegate is now a recommended delegate of TTURLRequest.
    
    This allows cool things like passing a class as a delegate. Look forward
    to more changes like this in the future.
    
    The tradeoff here is that we don't get as many compile-time checks for
    proper implementation of the delegate.
    - You still get warnings if your class implements a delegate, but is missing
    some required methods.
    - You won't get warnings when you assign an object that doesn't implement a
    delegate.

commit 957e549a6536cd60e6ec4b16558e2672fc61331c
Author: uprise78 <desaro@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Nov 15 19:49:34 2009 -0800

    added date formatter for a smaller, relative format that goes back up to 1 week before defaulting to mm/dd/yyy

commit 1f14b7578ae4c3e0a926087606fd79d0c56bd2af
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 8 13:52:33 2009 -0800

    [BugFix] Fix NSArray's containsObject method.
    
    performSelector: will return a value of type id. This caused difficult
    to repro bugs in containsObject's use of performSelector: with methods
    that return type BOOL (an unsigned char). This was because the method
    would return an unsigned char, but this would then be cast to id
    (a four-byte variable). This left room for uninitialized data in the
    top three bytes of the variable, effectively causing containsObject to
    always return true.

commit 1404c7b5a424da668f768e54437af14b83618ebc
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Nov 25 19:08:29 2009 -0800

    Add a synchronous request implementation to TTURLRequest.
    
    Synchronous requests allow you to make network requests from
    multi-threaded apps without dealing with locks. You can now make synchronous
    requests by calling sendSynchronously on a TTURLRequest object.
    
    Testing: Make a synchronous request using TTURLRequest. All of your standard
    delegate methods should still be called.
    This change should not affect synchronous requests.
    
    Example code:
    TTURLRequest* request = [TTURLRequest requestWithURL:URL delegate:self];
    [request sendSynchronously];

commit 4358c22b1d3b9bfb04a60d7bfce79b026de7ba4c
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Nov 23 16:39:28 2009 -0800

    Add TTHighlightBorderStyle and improve TTReflectiveFillStyle's algorithm.
    
    TTHighlightBorderStyle is a border with a semi-transparent highlight
    border drawn one pixel down and beneath the outer border. This makes
    it possible to simulate the style of the "Delete Contact" button found in
    the Contacts app.
    
    TTReflectiveFillStyle's algorithm was just plain broken; it used a mashup of
    hand-picked HSV numbers to "tint" the edge of the gradient. This change simply
    draws a semi-transparent white gradient on top of the fill color. It also
    adds a subtle, semi-transparent gradient to the bottom of the fill to complete
    the bubble illusion.
    
    Added:
    + (TTReflectiveFillStyle*)styleWithColor:(UIColor*)color
                              withBottomHighlight:(BOOL)withBottomHighlight
                              next:(TTStyle*)next
    
    If the original styleWithColor:next: method is used, withBottomHighlight
    defaults to NO.
    
    Testing: Open TTCatalog and check out the styled views. The two nav-bar styles
    should still have a nice gradient.

commit 8d4e1c76a608831d93e67de5b9588b134b833e9b
Author: Owen Yamauchi <oyamauchi@facebook.com>
Date:   Fri Nov 20 15:48:32 2009 -0800

    Fix hardcoded cache expiration age 0 meaning "never"
    
    With 6d3c266, expiration age 0 no longer signifies an object that never expires,
    so this case was broken. Use floating-point infinity for "never" (and yes, that
    trick works on all architectures; it's in IEEE 754).

commit 8695f299ec7ab5525e0e4081a996ca466f511537
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Nov 17 20:29:29 2009 -0800

    [ISSUE 85] - TTLauncherView - Switching to editing mode when there's only one TTLauncherItem
    
    Fix sleuthed by github.com/uprise78, amended to avoid dangling UIView animations.
    
    The problem:
    UIView animations will immediately call the delegate on commitAnimations if nothing was actually
    animated.
    
    This caused a problem in the launcherview due to the fact that -wobble used itself as the
    delegate to repeat the animation, causing infinite recursion when the launcher view was empty.
    This fix counts the number of affected views and then only adds the -wobble delegate to the
    animation if any views will actually be animated.
    
    This differs from uprise78's original fix in that we now always commit the animation to avoid
    unintentional nested UIView animation calls.
    
    The original fix can be found here:
    http://github.com/facebook/three20/issues#issue/85

commit 6d3c266972d6c471bb62a223592fd9333d72c4df
Author: Jeff Verkoeyen <jverkoey@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Nov 17 20:20:03 2009 -0800

    [ISSUE 67] - Infinite loop when notifying model delegates of load start when the model is outdated
    
    Part 1:
      Set the default cache expiration date for TTURLRequests to TT_DEFAULT_CACHE_EXPIRATION_AGE.
    
    Part 2 (and why it's necessary):
    The infinite loop occurs specifically when the model is outdated and the cache expirationdate
    is set to 0. This causes a problem in
    - (NSData*)dataForKey:(NSString*)key expires:(NSTimeInterval)expirationAge
       timestamp:(NSDate**)timestamp
    because it will only return a miss on the data if expirationAge is non-zero. This doesn't make
    intuitive sense because if the expirationAge is 0, any file should technically result in
    a miss and be re-requested. This change considers expirationAge properly.
    
    Paired with the default expiration age and the fix to cache misses, the cache should now properly
    execute a miss on expired data without being excessive (the default expiration age is 1 week).
